This also means that the work\\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\\n190:      * <p>\\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\\n194:      *\\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\\n197:      */\\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\\n200:     }\\n201: \\n202:     /**\\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\\n204:      * The {@code \\\"auto.offset.reset\\\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\\n206:      * <p>\\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. used.\\n231:      * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\\n232:      * <p>\\n233:      * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\\n234:      * // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\\n256:      * }</pre>\\n257:      * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\\n258:      * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\\n259:      *\\n260:      * @param topic              the topic name; This also means that the work\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n190:      * <p>\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n194:      *\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n197:      */\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     /**\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n204:      * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n206:      * <p>\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n230:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n231:      * Input {@link KeyValue Because the source topic can\n239:      * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n240:      * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n241:      * <p>\n242:      * You should only specify serdes in the {@link Consumed} instance as these will also be used to overwrite the\n243:      * serdes in {@link Materialized}, i.e.,\n244:      * <pre> {@code\n245:      * streamBuilder.table(topic, Consumed.with(Serde.String(), Serde.String()), Materialized.<String, String, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>as(storeName))\n246:      * }\n247:      * </pre>\n248:      * To query the local {@link ReadOnlyKeyValueStore} it must be obtained via\n249:      * {@link KafkaStreams#store(StoreQueryParameters) KafkaStreams#store(...)}:\n250:      * <pre>{@code\n251:      * KafkaStreams streams = ...\n252:      * StoreQueryParameters<ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>>> storeQueryParams = StoreQueryParameters.fromNameAndType(queryableStoreName, QueryableStoreTypes.timestampedKeyValueStore());\n253:      * ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>> localStore = streams.store(storeQueryParams);\n254:      * K key = \"some-key\";\n255:      * ValueAndTimestamp<V> valueForKey = localStore.get(key); // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n256:      * }</pre>\n257:      * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n258:      * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n259:      *\n260:      * @param topic              the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n263:      * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n264:      */\n265:     public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n266:                                                   final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\n267:                                                   final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n268:         Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n269:         Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n270:         Objects.requireNonNull(materialized, \"materialized can't be null\");\n271:         final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal = new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed);\n272:         materialized.withKeySerde(consumedInternal.keySerde()).withValueSerde(consumedInternal.valueSerde());\n273: \n274:         final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n275:             new MaterializedInternal<>(materialized, internalStreamsBuilder, topic + \"-\");\n276: \n277:         return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n278:     }\n279: \n280:     /**\n281:      * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n282:      * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy and default key and value deserializers as specified in the\n283:      * {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n284:      * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n285:      * <p>\n286:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n287:      * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n288:      * <p>\n289:      * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n290:      * store name. ValueTransformers}\n522:      * before they can be used.\n523:      *\n524:      * @param builder the builder used to obtain this state store {@link StateStore} instance\n525:      * @return itself\n526:      * @throws TopologyException if state store supplier is already added\n527:      */\n528:     public synchronized StreamsBuilder addStateStore(final StoreBuilder<?> builder) {\n529:         Objects.requireNonNull(builder, \"builder can't be null\");\n530:         internalStreamsBuilder.addStateStore(StoreBuilderWrapper.wrapStoreBuilder(builder));\n531:         return this;\n532:     }\n533: \n534:     /**\n535:      * Adds a global {@link StateStore} to the topology.\n536:      * The {@link StateStore} sources its data from all partitions of the provided input topic.\n537:      * There will be exactly one instance of this {@link StateStore} per Kafka Streams instance.\n538:      * <p>\n539:      * A {@link SourceNode} with the provided sourceName will be added to consume the data arriving from the partitions\n540:      * of the input topic.\n541:      * <p>\n542:      * The provided {@link ProcessorSupplier} will be used to create an\n543:      * {@link Processor} that will receive all records forwarded from the {@link SourceNode}.\n544:      * The supplier should always generate a new instance. Creating a single {@link Processor} object\n545:      * and returning the same object reference in {@link ProcessorSupplier#get()} is a\n546:      * violation of the supplier pattern and leads to runtime exceptions.\n547:      * This {@link Processor} should be used to keep the {@link StateStore} up-to-date.\n548:      * The default {@link TimestampExtractor} as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} is used.\n549:      * <p>\n550:      * It is not required to connect a global store to the {@link Processor Processors},\n551:      * or {@link org.apache.kafka.streams.kstream.KTable#transformValues(ValueTransformerWithKeySupplier, String...) ValueTransformer};\n552:      * those have read-only access to all global stores by default.\n553:      *\n554:      * @param storeBuilder          user defined {@link StoreBuilder}; can't be {@code already registered\n560:      */\n561:     public synchronized <KIn, VIn> StreamsBuilder addGlobalStore(final StoreBuilder<?> storeBuilder,\n562:                                                                  final String topic,\n563:                                                                  final Consumed<KIn, VIn> consumed,\n564:                                                                  final ProcessorSupplier<KIn, VIn, Void, Void> stateUpdateSupplier) {\n565:         Objects.requireNonNull(storeBuilder, \"storeBuilder can't be null\");\n566:
